<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="rapid-acting-insulin">Rapid-acting insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#rapid-acting-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Three injected rapid-acting insulin analogues:</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>insulin lispro</li>
<li>insulin aspart</li>
<li>insulin glulisine</li>
<li>An inhaled form of rapid-acting insulin, human insulin recombinant inhaled</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Onset of action 5-15 min.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Duration of action 3-5 hours, exception of inhaled insulin which may last 6-7 hrs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This short duration ↓ the risk of late post meal hypoglycemia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They permit more physiologic <strong>prandial insulin replacement</strong> owing to their rapid onset and early peak action that more closely mimic normal endogenous <strong>prandial insulin secretion</strong>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They have the additional benefit of allowing insulin to be taken immediately before the meal without sacrificing glucose control.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The injected rapid acting insulin has the lowest variability of absorption (5%) of all available commercial insulins compared to 25% for regular and 25-50% for intermediate long acting formulation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Are there preferred for use in continuous SC insulin and infusion devices.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="short-acting-insulin">Short-acting insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#short-acting-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Two types</li>
<li>Regular insulin</li>
<li>Semi - lente insulin
A. Regular insulin: is a short-acting soluble crystalline zinc insulin made by recombinant DNA techniques to produce a molecule identical to human insulin</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-regular-insulin">a) Regular insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-regular-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Is used intravenous in emergencies administered SC in ordinary maintenance regimen</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Can be given alone or mixed with intermediate or long acting preparation.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Given 30-45 min before meal its effect within 30 minutes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Peak 2-3 hrs,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Regular insulin is used intravenously in management &amp; DKA &amp; when the insulin requirement is rapidly e.g. in surgery.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>b) Semi-lente insulin (prompt insulin zinc suspension)</p>
<ul>
<li>Rarely used</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="nb">NB//<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#nb" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>After subcutaneous injection, the insulin hexamers are too large and bulky to be transported across the vascular endothelium into the bloodstream</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The insulin depot is diluted by interstitial fluid and the concentration begins to fall, the hexamers break down into dimers and finally monomers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>As a result, it display 3 rates of absorption</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The final phase having the fastest uptake out of the injection site</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When regular insulin is administered at mealtime, the blood glucose rises faster than the insulin with resultant early postprandial hyperglycemia and an increased risk of late postprandial hypoglycemia</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The delayed absorption results in a mismatching of insulin availability with need</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Regular insulin should be injected 30-45 or more minutes before the meal to minimize the mismatching</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The duration of action as well as the time of onset and the intensity of peak action increase with the size of the dose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Short-acting soluble insulin is the only type that should be administered intravenously because the dilution causes the hexameric insulin to immediately dissociate into monomers</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It is particularly useful for intravenous therapy in the management of diabetic ketoacidosis and when the insulin requirement is changing rapidly, such as after surgery or during acute infections</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="intermediate-acting-and-long-acting-insulins">Intermediate-acting and long-acting insulins<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#intermediate-acting-and-long-acting-insulins" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>NPH (neutral protamine Hagedorn, or isophane) insulin- intermediate acting</li>
<li>Insulin glargine- ultra long acting</li>
<li>Insulin detemir- long acting</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-neutral-protamine-hagedorn-nph-or-isophane-insulin">A. Neutral protamine Hagedorn(NPH) or isophane insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-neutral-protamine-hagedorn-nph-or-isophane-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Absorption and onset of action are delayed by combining appropriate amount of insulin with protamine (Ratio 1:10 by weight, for protamine : insulin)</li>
<li>Usually mixed with regular, lispro, aspart, or glulisine insulin</li>
<li>Administered two to four times daily for insulin replacement in patients with type 1 diabetes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="lente-insulin">Lente-insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#lente-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Intermediate acting insulin</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Mixture of 30% semilente and 70% ultra lente</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has delayed onset and long period of action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The dose regulates the action profile; specifically, small doses have lower, earlier peaks and a short duration of action with the converse true for large doses</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Onset of action 2-5 hrs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Peaks within 4-6hrs</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Duration of action 4-12 hrs</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-insulin-glargine">B. Insulin Glargine<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-insulin-glargine" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>An ultra long acting soluble, "peakless" i.e have a broad plasma concentration plateau), ultra-long-acting insulin analog</li>
<li>Soluble in an acidic solution but precipitates in the more neutral body pH after subcutaneous injection</li>
<li>Provide a low, continuous level of circulating insulin</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="insulin-glargine-ct">Insulin glargine ct.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin-glargine-ct" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Has a slow onset of action (1-1.5 hours) and achieves a maximum effect after 4-6 hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maximum activity is maintained for 11-24 hours or longer</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Usually given once daily, very insulin-sensitive individuals benefit from split (twice a day) dosing</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Should not be mixed with other insulins</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Separate syringes must be used to minimize the risk of contamination and subsequent loss of efficacy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Absorption pattern appears to be independent of the anatomic site of injection,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Associated with less immunogenicity than human insulin</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="c-insulin-detemir">c. Insulin detemir<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-insulin-detemir" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>A long-acting insulin analog</li>
<li>Its use is associated with less hypoglycemia than NPH insulin</li>
<li>Has a dose-dependent onset of action of 1-2 hours</li>
<li>Duration of action is more than 24 hours</li>
<li>Given twice daily to obtain a smooth background insulin level
NB Not mixable with other insulins</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="protamine-zinc-insulin">Protamine Zinc insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#protamine-zinc-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Are human insulin</li>
<li>Long acting insulin</li>
<li>Onset of action 4-6hrs peak activity 14-18hrs duration of action of 24-36hrs.</li>
<li>Often given in the morning or morning &amp; evening to provide maintenance of or basal insulin levels. This may be supplemented by individual injection of rapid actions or short acting during the day to meet the requirement of CHO intake.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mixtures-of-insulin">Mixtures of insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mixtures-of-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>intermediate-acting NPH insulins require several hours to reach adequate therapeutic levels,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Their use in type 1 diabetic patients requires supplements of rapid- or short-acting insulin before meals</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For convenience, these are often mixed together in the same syringe before injection</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insulin lispro, aspart, and glulisine can be acutely mixed (ie, just before injection) with NPH insulin without affecting their rapid absorption</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Premixed preparations have been unstable</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Neutral protamine lispro (NPL) and neutral protamine aspart (NPA) have the same duration of action as NPH insulin are intermediate insulin that are premixed combinations of NPL and insulin lispro, and as NPA and insulin aspart respectively</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="complication-of-insulin-therapy">Complication of Insulin Therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#complication-of-insulin-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>1.Hypoglycemia - the most common complications</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="occur-due-to-due-to">Occur due to due to;<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#occur-due-to-due-to" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Delay in taking meal</li>
<li>Inadequate CHO consumption</li>
<li>Unusual physical exertion</li>
<li>A dose of insulin too large for immediate needs</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="managing-hypoglycemia">Managing hypoglycemia<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#managing-hypoglycemia" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Relieved by glucose administration</li>
<li>Simple sugar or glucose given in liquid form</li>
<li>Patients who can swallow be given dextrose tablets, glucose gel, or any sugar containing beverage or food</li>
<li>Honey syrup into the bucal pouch can be used</li>
<li>If patient is unconscious or in a stupor, give 20-50 ml of 50% dextrose IV over 2-3 min or 1 mg of glucagon subcutaneously or IM</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-immunological-effect">2. Immunological effect<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-immunological-effect" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Insulin induced immunologic complication</li>
<li>5 molecular classes of insulin antibodies may result during therapy: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mi>lg</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>A</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>lg</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>D</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>lg</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>E</mi><mo separator="true">,</mo><mi>lg</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>G</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">&amp;</mi><mi>lg</mi><mo>⁡</mo><mi>M</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\lg A, \lg D, \lg E, \lg G \&amp; \lg M</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8889em; vertical-align: -0.1944em;"></span><span class="mop">l<span style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">A</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">l<span style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.02778em;">D</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">l<span style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.05764em;">E</span><span class="mpunct">,</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">l<span style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal">G</span><span class="mord">&amp;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mop">l<span style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">g</span></span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.1667em;"></span><span class="mord mathnormal" style="margin-right: 0.10903em;">M</span></span></span></span></span>
a. Insulin allergy: An immediate hypersensitivity insulin</li>
<li>Anti- insulin IgE antibodies produced
b. Immune insulin resistance - anti-insulin igG antibodies neutralizes action of insulin</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-lipodystrophy">3.Lipodystrophy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-lipodystrophy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Atrophy of sc fatty tissue at injection site</li>
<li>Occur more with animal insulin</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="insulin-delivery-system">Insulin delivery system<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin-delivery-system" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>SC injection with conventional disposable syringes and needles- more convenient and available- the standard mode of insulin therapy</li>
<li>Portable pen size injectors</li>
<li>Continuous subcutaneous insulin infusion device- an open loop pump for insulin delivery</li>
<li>Inhaled formulation of insulin can be used to cover meal time insulin requirements</li>
<li>Dose: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.5</mn><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.5-1 / \mathrm{Kg} /</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">0.5</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">1/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">Kg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span></span></span></span></span> day stat &amp; then adjust accordingly this given in multiple doses.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-end">THE END<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-end" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-864a055a.jpeg" alt="img-10.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="oral-antidiabetic-agents">ORAL ANTIDIABETIC AGENTS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#oral-antidiabetic-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Mwenda</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="introduction">Introduction<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#introduction" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Four major</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Insulin secretagogues -sulfonylureas, meglitinides, Dphenylalanine derivatives</li>
<li>Biguanides</li>
<li>Thiazolidinediones</li>
<li>Alpha-glucosidase inhibitors</li>
<li>Other</li>
</ol>
<blockquote>
<p>Pramlintide,
exenatide and
sitagliptin</p>
</blockquote>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-insulin-secretagogues">1. INSULIN SECRETAGOGUES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-insulin-secretagogues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-mechanism-and-effects-insulin">a) Mechanism and effects- Insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-mechanism-and-effects-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Secretagogues stimulate the release of endogenous insulin by promoting closure of potassium channels in the pancreatic B cell membrane.</li>
<li>Channel closure depolarizes the cell and triggers insulin release.</li>
<li>Insulin secretagogues are not effective in patients who lack functional pancreatic B cells.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="insulin-secretagogues">INSULIN SECRETAGOGUES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin-secretagogues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-64f36a8a.jpeg" alt="img-11.jpeg"></p>
<p><strong>Source:</strong> Katzung BG, Masters SB, Trevor AJ: <em>Basic &amp; Clinical Pharmacology, 11th Edition</em>; <a href="http://www.accessmedicine.com" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">http://www.accessmedicine.com</a></p>
<p><strong>Copyright ©</strong> The McGraw-Hill Companies, Inc. All rights reserved.</p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="1-insulin-secretagogues">1. INSULIN SECRETAGOGUES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#1-insulin-secretagogues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="a-mechanism-and-effects-insulin">a) Mechanism and effects- Insulin<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-mechanism-and-effects-insulin" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>Secretagogues stimulate the release of endogenous insulin by promoting closure of potassium channels in the pancreatic B cell membrane.</li>
<li>Channel closure depolarizes the cell and triggers insulin release.
NB// Insulin secretagogues are not effective in patients who lack functional pancreatic B cells.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="a-sulfonylureas">A. SULFONYLUREAS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#a-sulfonylureas" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>There are 2 groups</li>
</ul>
<p>1 <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mrow></mrow><mtext>st&nbsp;</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{ }^{\text {st }}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7936em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7936em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">st&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> generation sulfonylureas; older agents
a) Tolbutamide
b) Chlorpropamide</p>
<p>2 <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mrow></mrow><mtext>nd&nbsp;</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{ }^{\text {nd }}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord"></span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">nd&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> generation sulfonylureas
c) Glyburide,
d) Glipzide
e) Glimepiride</p>
<p>Are considerably more potent and used more commonly than the older agents</p>
<ul>
<li>Have a rapid onset and short duration of action</li>
<li>Administered just before a meal (to control postprandial glucose levels)</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tolbutamide-orinase">Tolbutamide (Orinase)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tolbutamide-orinase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>1</mn><mtext>st&nbsp;</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">1^{\text {st }}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7936em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">1</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7936em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">st&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> generation</li>
<li>Well absorbed</li>
<li>Rapidly metabolized in the liver</li>
<li>Its duration of effect is relatively short, with an elimination half-life of 4-5 hours</li>
<li>Best administered in divided doses</li>
<li>Because of its short half-life, it is the safest sulfonylurea for elderly diabetics</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adrs">ADRs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Prolonged hypoglycemia has been reported rarely, mostly in patients receiving certain drugs that inhibit the metabolism of tolbutamide e.g, dicumarol, phenylbutazone, some sulfonamides) that</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="chlorpropamide-diabinese">Chlorpropamide (diabinese)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#chlorpropamide-diabinese" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Half-life of 32 hours</li>
<li>Slowly metabolized in the liver to products that retain some biologic activity</li>
<li>Approximately 20-30% is excreted unchanged in the urine</li>
<li>Contraindicated in patients with hepatic or renal insufficiency</li>
<li>Dosages higher than 500 mg daily increase the risk of jaundice</li>
<li>The average maintenance dosage is 250 mg daily, given as a single dose in the morning</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adrs">ADRs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Prolonged hypoglycemic reactions are more common in elderly patients, and the drug is contraindicated in this group</li>
<li>Hyperemic flush after alcohol ingestion in genetically predisposed patients and dilutional hyponatremia</li>
<li>Hematologic toxicity (transient leukopenia, thrombocytopenia) occurs in less than 1% of patients</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="tolazamide-tolinase">Tolazamide (tolinase)<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#tolazamide-tolinase" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Comparable to chlorpropamide in potency but has a shorter duration of action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>More slowly absorbed than the other sulfonylureas</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Its effect on blood glucose does not appear for several hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Its half-life is about 7 hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is metabolized to several compounds that retain hypoglycemic effects</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>If more than <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>500</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">500 \mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{d}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">500</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">d</span></span></span></span></span> are required, the dose should be divided and given twice daily</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Have fewer adverse effects and drug interactions</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Include:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<ol>
<li>Glipizide</li>
<li>Glimepiride</li>
</ol>
<ul>
<li>should be used with caution in patients with cardiovascular disease or in elderly patients, in whom hypoglycemia would be especially dangerous</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="glyburide">Glyburide<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glyburide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Metabolized in the liver into products with very low hypoglycemic activity.</li>
<li>The usual starting dosage is <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>2.5</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2.5 \mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{d}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">2.5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">d</span></span></span></span></span> or less, and the average maintenance dosage is 5-10 <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{d}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">d</span></span></span></span></span> given as a single morning dose</li>
<li>Available in a variety of tablet sizes</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adrs">ADRs:<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Potential for causing hypoglycemia</li>
<li>Flushing has rarely been reported after ethanol ingestion</li>
<li>Slightly enhances free water clearance</li>
</ul>
<p>Contraindication:</p>
<ol>
<li>Hepatic impairment</li>
<li>Patients with renal insufficiency</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="glipizide">Glipizide<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glipizide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Half-life ;2-4 hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>For maximum effect in reducing postprandial hyperglycemia, this agent should be ingested 30 minutes before breakfast- absorption is delayed when the drug is taken with food</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The recommended starting dosage is <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>5</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">5 \mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{d}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">5</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">d</span></span></span></span></span>, with up to <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>15</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">15 \mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{d}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">15</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord mathrm">d</span></span></span></span></span> given as a single dose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When higher daily dosages are required, they should be divided and given before meals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Maximum recommended total daily dose- 40 mg/d</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>An extended-release preparation - Glucotrol XL provides 24-hour action after a once-daily morning dose</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At least 90% of glipizide is metabolized in the liver to inactive products,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>10% is excreted unchanged in the urine</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Contraindication: in patients with significant hepatic or renal impairment- coz of high risk for hypoglycemia</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="glimepiride">Glimepiride<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#glimepiride" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Given once-daily as monotherapy or in combination with insulin: A single daily dose of 1 mg</li>
<li>Achieves blood glucose lowering with the lowest dose of any sulfonylurea compound</li>
<li>The recommended maximal daily dose is 8 mg</li>
<li>Has a long duration of effect with a half-life of 5 hours, allowing once-daily dosing and thereby improving compliance</li>
<li>Completely metabolized by the liver to inactive products</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="b-meglitinides-insulin-secretagogues">B. MEGLITINIDES- INSULIN SECRETAGOGUES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#b-meglitinides-insulin-secretagogues" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>2ng grp of secretor gogues</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Repaglinide</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has a very fast onset of action,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Peak concentration and peak effect within 1 hour after ingestion,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Duration of action is 5-8 hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cleared hepatically</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Plasma half-life of 1 hour</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Indicated for use in controlling postprandial glucose excursions coz of it rapid onset of action</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Should be taken just before each meal in doses of 0.25-4 mg (maximum, 16 mg/d);</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypoglycemia is a risk if the meal is delayed or skipped or contains inadequate carbohydrate</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Should be used cautiously in individuals with renal and hepatic impairment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Approved as monotherapy or in combination with biguanides</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>There is no sulfur in its structure, so repaglinide may be used in type 2 diabetic individuals with sulfur or sulfonylurea allergy</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="c-d-phenylalanine-derivative">C. D-PHENYLALANINE DERIVATIVE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#c-d-phenylalanine-derivative" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Nateglinide: a D-phenylalanine derivative</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>MOA: Stimulates very rapid and transient release of insulin from B cells through closure of the ATP-sensitive <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mi mathvariant="normal">K</mi><mo lspace="0em" rspace="0em">+</mo></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{K}^{+}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7713em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">K</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.7713em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord mtight">+</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>channel</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>It also partially restores initial insulin release in response to an intravenous glucose tolerance test; a significant advantage of the drug because type 2 diabetes is associated with loss of this initial insulin response</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has a role in the treatment of individuals with isolated postprandial hyperglycemia,</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Has minimal effect on overnight or fasting glucose levels</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Efficacious when given alone or in combination with nonsecretagogue oral agents (such as metformin)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Dose titration is not required</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Ingested just before meals</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Absorbed rapidly- within 20 minutes after oral administration</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Time to peak concentration is less than 1 hour</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>hepatically metabolized &amp; has a half-life of 1.5 hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The overall duration of action is less than 4 hours</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nateglinide amplifies the insulin secretory response to a glucose load but has a markedly diminished effect in the presence of normal glucose levels;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Is Therefore safe in individuals with very reduced renal function</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="2-biguanides">2. BIGUANIDES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#2-biguanides" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>2</mn><mtext>nd&nbsp;</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">2^{\text {nd }}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">2</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">nd&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> grp; oral hypoglycemics</li>
<li>Eg. Metformin</li>
<li>Phenformin cause lactic acidosis and because therefore no longer in use</li>
<li>Biguanide therapy is not known to cause hypoglycemia</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="mechanisms-of-action">Mechanisms of Action<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#mechanisms-of-action" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Inhibit hepatic and renal gluconeogenesis</li>
</ul>
<p>Other effects include</p>
<ul>
<li>Stimulation of glucose in peripheral tissues</li>
<li>Slowing of glucose absorption from the gastrointestinal tract, and</li>
<li>Reduction of plasma glucagon levels</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="cont">CONT.<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#cont" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>In patients with insulin resistance, metformin reduces endogenous insulin production presumably through enhanced insulin sensitivity.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Does not increase weight (unlike insulin, secretagogues, or the thiazolidinediones)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Metformin is increasingly the drug of first choice in overweight patients with type 2 diabetes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Metformin is also used to restore fertility in anovulatory women with polycystic ovary disease (PCOD) and evidence of insulin resistance</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="toxicities">TOXICITIES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#toxicities" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>NB: Unlike the sulfonylureas, the biguanides do not cause hypoglycemia</li>
<li>Most common toxicity:GIT distress (nausea, diarrhea),</li>
<li>Can cause lactic acidosis, especially in patients with renal or liver disease, alcoholism, or conditions that predispose to tissue anoxia and lactic acid production (e.g. chronic cardiopulmonary dysfunction).</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="3-thiazolidinediones">3. THIAZOLIDINEDIONES<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#3-thiazolidinediones" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li><span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><msup><mn>3</mn><mtext>rd&nbsp;</mtext></msup></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">3^{\text {rd }}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8491em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord">3</span><span class="msupsub"><span class="vlist-t"><span class="vlist-r"><span class="vlist" style="height: 0.8491em;"><span style="top: -3.063em; margin-right: 0.05em;"><span class="pstrut" style="height: 2.7em;"></span><span class="sizing reset-size6 size3 mtight"><span class="mord mtight"><span class="mord text mtight"><span class="mord mtight">rd&nbsp;</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> oral hypoglycemic</li>
<li>Eg thiazolidinediones, rosiglitazone and pioglitazone</li>
<li>They are ligands of peroxisome proliferatoractivated receptor-gamma (PPAR-g), part of the steroid and thyroid superfamily of nuclear receptors]</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="moa">MOA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#moa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>They act to decrease insulin resistance: Their primary action is the regulation of genes involved in glucose and lipid metabolism and adipocyte differentiation</li>
<li>In the adipose tissue, they promotes glucose uptake and utilization and modulates synthesis of lipid hormones or cytokines and other proteins involved in energy regulation</li>
<li>Tzds also regulate adipocyte apoptosis and differentiation</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="4-alpha-glucosidase-inhibitors">4. ALPHA-GLUCOSIDASE INHIBITORS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#4-alpha-glucosidase-inhibitors" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Eg. Acarbose and miglitol</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>MOA:</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Only monosaccharides, such as glucose and fructose, can be transported out of the intestinal lumen and into the bloodstream</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Complex starches, oligosaccharides, and disaccharides must be broken down into individual monosaccharides before being absorbed in the duodenum and upper jejunum</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>This digestion is facilitated by enteric enzymes, including <strong>pancreatic α-amylase</strong>, and <strong>α-glucosidases</strong> that are attached to the brush border of the intestinal cells.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Acarbose</strong> and <strong>miglitol</strong> are competitive inhibitors of the intestinal α-glucosidases and reduce the postprandial digestion and absorption of starch and disaccharides.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>They therefore minimize upper intestinal digestion and defer digestion and thus absorption of the ingested starch and disaccharides to the distal small intestine, thereby lowering postmeal glycemic excursions and creating an insulin-sparing effect</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Monotherapy with these drugs is associated with a modest drop ( <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>0.5</mn><mo>−</mo><mn>1</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">0.5-1 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.7278em; vertical-align: -0.0833em;"></span><span class="mord">0.5</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span><span class="mbin">−</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2222em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">1%</span></span></span></span></span> ) in glycohemoglobin levels and a fall in fasting glucose levels</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Taken in doses of 25-100 mg just before ingesting the first portion of each meal; therapy should be initiated with the lowest dose and slowly titrated upward</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Can be used as monotherapy or in combination with sulfonylureas in type 2 diabetes an, in which the glycemic effect is additive</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="adrs">Adrs<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#adrs" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>Flatulence, diarrhea, and abdominal pain- result from the appearance of undigested carbohydrate in the colon that is then fermented into short-chain fatty acids, releasing gas- tend to diminish with ongoing use (because chronic exposure to carbohydrate induces the expression of a-glucosidase in the jejunum and ileum, increasing distal small intestine glucose absorption and minimizing the passage of carbohydrate into the colon)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Hypoglycemia may occur with concurrent sulfonylurea treatment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>should be treated with glucose (dextrose) and not sucrose whose breakdown may be blocked</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Contraindications: Patients with inflammatory bowel disease or any intestinal condition that could be worsened by gas and distention</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Both (miglitol and acarbose) are excreted by the kidneys, and should not be prescribed in individuals with renal impairment</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Acarbose has been associated with reversible hepatic enzyme elevation and should be used with caution in the presence of hepatic disease</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="others-hypoglycemic-agents">Others hypoglycemic agents<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#others-hypoglycemic-agents" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ol>
<li>PRAMLINTIDE</li>
<li>EXENATIDE</li>
<li>SITAGLIPTIN</li>
</ol>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="pramlintide">PRAMLINTIDE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#pramlintide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Given as a subcutaneous injection</li>
<li>Modulates postprandial glucose levels</li>
<li>Approved for preprandial use in individuals with type 1 and type 2 diabetes</li>
<li>It is administered in addition to insulin in those individuals who are unable to achieve their target postprandial blood sugars</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="moa">MOA<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#moa" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Suppresses glucagon release</li>
<li>Delays gastric emptying, and</li>
<li>Has central nervous system-mediated anorectic effects</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="exenatide">EXENATIDE<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#exenatide" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>An injectable adjunctive therapy in individuals with type 2 diabetes treated with metformin or sulfonylureas who still have suboptimal glycemic control</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Injected subcutaneously within 60 minutes before a meal</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Therapy is initiated at 5 mcg twice daily, with a maximum dosage of 10 mcg twice daily.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>When exenatide is added to preexisting sulfonylurea therapy, the oral hypoglycemic dosage may need to be decreased to prevent hypoglycemia.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>ADRs: The major side effects are nausea (about <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>44</mn><mi mathvariant="normal">%</mi></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">44 \%</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.8056em; vertical-align: -0.0556em;"></span><span class="mord">44%</span></span></span></span></span> of users) and vomiting and diarrhea.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Nausea decreases with ongoing usage</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="summary">Summary<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#summary" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="combination-therapy">Combination therapy<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#combination-therapy" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li>
<p>There is no indication for combining insulin with insulin secretagogues (sulfonylureas, meglitinides, or D-phenylalanine derivatives) in individuals with type 1 diabetes</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Type 1 diabetics with diets very high in starch may benefit from the addition of a-glucosidase inhibitors</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Bedtime insulin has been suggested as an adjunct to oral antidiabetic therapy in patients with type 2 diabetes patients who have not responded to maximal oral therapy</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Individuals unable to achieve glycemic control with bedtime insulin generally require full insulin replacement and multiple daily injections of insulin</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Insulin secretagogues are redundant when an individual is receiving multiple daily insulin injections</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Multiple oral agents have been required together with insulin in some cases</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="the-end">THE END<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#the-end" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-a985f52f.jpeg" alt="img-12.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="insulin-and-diabetes-mellitus">INSULIN AND DIABETES MELLITUS<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#insulin-and-diabetes-mellitus" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>1921Banting and Best</li>
<li>1923 Nobel Prize (sharing)</li>
<li>1926 crystalline form obtained by Abel</li>
<li>1956-69 chemical and molecular structure was worked out by Sanger and Hodgkin.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="charles-h-best-frederick-g-banting">CHARLES H. BEST &amp; FREDERICK G. BANTING<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#charles-h-best-frederick-g-banting" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<p>Dog, Margorie was injected with the first insulin in 1921</p>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-a4bbee84.jpeg" alt="img-13.jpeg"></p>
<ul>
<li>Alpha cells : Glucagon</li>
<li>Beta Cells : Insulin</li>
<li>Delta Cells : Gastrin</li>
<li>Normal range of Blood glucose: 70 - 120 <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">(</mo><mn>100</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow><mo stretchy="false">)</mo></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{dl}(100 \mathrm{ml})</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">dl</span></span><span class="mopen">(</span><span class="mord">100</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">ml</span></span><span class="mclose">)</span></span></span></span></span></li>
<li>Hypoglycemia: <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mo>&lt;</mo><mn>70</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">&lt;70 \mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{dl}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 0.5782em; vertical-align: -0.0391em;"></span><span class="mrel">&lt;</span><span class="mspace" style="margin-right: 0.2778em;"></span></span><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">70</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">dl</span></span></span></span></span></span></li>
<li>Diabetes: &gt; <span class="math math-inline"><span class="katex"><span class="katex-mathml"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><semantics><mrow><mn>120</mn><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">g</mi></mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">/</mi><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">d</mi><mi mathvariant="normal">l</mi></mrow></mrow><annotation encoding="application/x-tex">120 \mathrm{mg} / \mathrm{dl}</annotation></semantics></math></span><span class="katex-html" aria-hidden="true"><span class="base"><span class="strut" style="height: 1em; vertical-align: -0.25em;"></span><span class="mord">120</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm" style="margin-right: 0.01389em;">mg</span></span><span class="mord">/</span><span class="mord"><span class="mord mathrm">dl</span></span></span></span></span></span> overnight fasting, 23 hr after meal.</li>
</ul>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="regulation-of-normal-blood-sugar">Regulation of Normal blood sugar<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#regulation-of-normal-blood-sugar" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h2 level="2" id="low-blood-glucose">Low Blood Glucose<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#low-blood-glucose" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h2></div>
<ul>
<li><strong>Gastrin form delta cells</strong></li>
<li><strong>Pancreas (islets of langerhans)</strong></li>
<li><strong>Glucagon Released by Alpha Cells of Pancreas</strong></li>
<li><strong>Liver Releases Glucose into Blood</strong></li>
<li><strong>Insulin Released by Beta Cells of Pancreas</strong></li>
<li><strong>Fat Cells Take in Glucose from Blood</strong></li>
<li><strong>Achieve Normal Blood Glucose Levels</strong></li>
</ul>
<p><img src="assets/images/image-20251214-6af81a55.jpeg" alt="img-14.jpeg"></p>
<div data-testid="stHeadingWithActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-1p9ibxm e1icttdg2"><h1 level="1" id="diabetes-mellitus-definition">Diabetes Mellitus Definition<span data-testid="stHeaderActionElements" class="st-emotion-cache-gi0tri e1icttdg3"><a href="#diabetes-mellitus-definition" class="st-emotion-cache-yinll1 e1icttdg1"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="16" height="16" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round"><path d="M15 7h3a5 5 0 0 1 5 5 5 5 0 0 1-5 5h-3m-6 0H6a5 5 0 0 1-5-5 5 5 0 0 1 5-5h3"></path><line x1="8" y1="12" x2="16" y2="12"></line></svg></a></span></h1></div>
<ul>
<li>Is a group of metabolic diseases characterized by increased levels of glucose in the blood (hyperglycemia) resulting from defects in insulin secretion, insulin action, or both</li>
<li>related to:</li>
<li>An endocrine disorder causes Abnormal insulin production</li>
<li>Impaired insulin utilization</li>
<li>Both abnormal production and impaired utilization</li>
</ul>

<p>KNOW THE SYMPTOMS
